# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary of Findings

I've identified and documented all the key Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the GroupCoordinator, including:

**Core Coordinator Components:**
- GroupCoordinator interface and service implementations
- GroupCoordinatorShard for per-partition coordination
- GroupMetadataManager as the central implementation
- GroupCoordinatorConfig for configuration management

**Group State Machine:**
- ClassicGroupState enum defining the five states: Empty, PreparingRebalance, CompletingRebalance, Stable, and Dead
- Valid state transition rules embedded in the state machine

**Request Handlers:**
- JoinGroup/SyncGroup handlers for classic protocol
- Consumer/Streams/Share group heartbeat handlers for modern protocols
- Entry points in KafkaApis.scala that route requests to the coordinator

**Group Implementations:**
- Classic groups (ClassicGroup, ClassicGroupMember)
- Modern consumer groups (ConsumerGroup, ConsumerGroupMember)
- Streams groups (StreamsGroup, StreamsGroupMember)
- Share groups (ShareGroup, ShareGroupMember)

**Heartbeat Expiry Detection:**
- Timeout scheduling and cancellation mechanisms
- Member heartbeat expiration handling (expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat)
- Automatic rescheduling of heartbeat timeouts
- Separate timeout configurations for each group protocol type

The answer includes complete file paths, relevant symbol names, the request processing chain, and a comprehensive narrative explanation of how the system works.

protocol with leader-based assignment\\n2. **Consumer Group** (ConsumerGroup.java, ConsumerGroupMember.java): Modern consumer protocol with cooperative rebalancing\\n3. **Streams Group** The core interface is defined in GroupCoordinator.java, which specifies the contract for group coordination operations including JoinGroupRequest and SyncGroupRequest handling for both classic and modern (consumer, streams, share) group protocols, and heartbeat management.\\n\\n## Group State Machine\\nThe classic group protocol uses a finite state machine defined in ClassicGroupState.java with five states:\\n- Empty: Group has no members, awaiting new members\\n- PreparingRebalance: Members are joining, group is preparing for rebalance\\n- CompletingRebalance: Leader has provided assignment, awaiting sync from all members\\n- Stable: All members are synchronized with assignments\\n- Dead: Group is being deleted\\n\\nState transitions are validated in ClassicGroupState.java (lines 111-117) which define valid previous states for each state.\\n\\n## Request Handlers\\nThe request flow is orchestrated through:\\n1. GroupCoordinatorService.java - Service layer implementation\\n   - handleJoinGroupRequest: Delegates to GroupCoordinatorShard for classic groups\\n   - handleSyncGroupRequest: Delegates to GroupCoordinatorShard for classic groups\\n   - consumerGroupHeartbeat/shareGroupHeartbeat/streamsGroupHeartbeat: Handle modern protocol heartbeats\\n\\n3. expireClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat (line 6664): Handles heartbeat timeout expiration for classic groups\\n- rescheduleClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat (line 7047 and 7061): Reschedules member heartbeat timeouts\\n\\n## Group Implementations\\nFour distinct group protocol implementations are provided:\\n\\n1. **Classic Group** (ClassicGroup.java, ClassicGroupMember.java): Traditional consumer group protocol with leader-based assignment\\n2. **Consumer Group** (ConsumerGroup.java, ConsumerGroupMember.java): Modern consumer protocol with cooperative rebalancing\\n3. **Streams Group** (StreamsGroup.java, StreamsGroupMember.java): Kafka Streams specific group protocol for topology management\\n4. **Share Group** (ShareGroup.java, ShareGroupMember.java): Share consumption protocol rescheduling via rescheduleClassicGroupMemberHeartbeat after successful heartbeats\\n\\nFor modern group protocols, heartbeat expiry is managed similarly through timer scheduling in
